  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_59e45ab7-ae0f-4b9f-b011-0e7c15313ea9'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer8956994366979108636">Seventeen-year-old Ruby is a Fireblood who has concealed her powers of heat and flame from the cruel Frostblood ruling class her entire life. But when her mother is killed trying to protect her, and rebel Frostbloods demand her help to overthrow their bloodthirsty king, she agrees to come out of hiding, desperate to have her revenge.<br/><br/>Despite her unpredictable abilities, Rub</span>
  <span id="freeText8956994366979108636" style="display:none">Seventeen-year-old Ruby is a Fireblood who has concealed her powers of heat and flame from the cruel Frostblood ruling class her entire life. But when her mother is killed trying to protect her, and rebel Frostbloods demand her help to overthrow their bloodthirsty king, she agrees to come out of hiding, desperate to have her revenge.<br /><br />Despite her unpredictable abilities, Ruby trains with the rebels and the infuriating - yet irresistible - Arcus, who seems to think of her as nothing more than a weapon. But before they can take action, Ruby is captured and forced to compete in the king’s tournaments that pit Fireblood prisoners against Frostblood champions. Now she has only one chance to destroy the maniacal ruler who has taken everything from her - and from the icy young man she has come to love.</span>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/807526-synopsis-sounds-like-red-queen-is-it">Synopsis sounds like Red Queen...is it like that book ?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_807526'><a id="like_count_community_question_807526" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/807526?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">7 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F27827203-frostblood">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/807526-synopsis-sounds-like-red-queen-is-it">4 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/807526-synopsis-sounds-like-red-queen-is-it">See all 7 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/5229386-alexa"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1603748371i/5229386._UY100_CR12,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/5229386-alexa">Alexa</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I'd say it diverges considerably from Red Queen despite a few common elements. The main character already knows about her power and works to master it<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I'd say it diverges considerably from Red Queen despite a few common elements. The main character already knows about her power and works to master it, as opposed to going from "ordinary" to "extraordinary" making for a different character arc. There's a slow building romance with lots of great tension--no love triangle (or square!). There's no revolution/big betrayals as plot devices--the MC, instead, has to explore her own darkness and desire for revenge. The writing style is also quite different. I'd consider Frostblood a "traditional" fantasy style/arc, whereas Red Queen is more "pop culture" fantasy (superpowers, etc.) meets dystopia style/arc. (Both books are great; just different)<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">No. The author does make reference to Gods but only in the creation-type of way. Blake explains how the Frostblood and Fireblood people came to existe<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">No. The author does make reference to Gods but only in the creation-type of way. Blake explains how the Frostblood and Fireblood people came to existence using these Gods but that is were it ends.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1768454913" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1768454913" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1768454913?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1768454913" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6591185287643704000">Have you read any mainstream YA fantasy book over the past few years? If so, it is likely you have already experienced this book with different character names.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27827203.Frostblood__Frostblood_Saga___1_' title='Frostblood (Frostblood Saga, #1) by Elly Blake' rel='nofollow noopener'>Frostblood</a> is just so... <b>unremarkable</b>. Everything about it is familiar and predictable, leading to a read that offered up no excitement, no need to keep turning the pages. It often feels as if YA fantasy publishers deliberately go looking for new authors to retell the same old recycled plots. Stick an attractive cover on the front and let</span>
  <span id="freeText6591185287643704000" style="display:none">Have you read any mainstream YA fantasy book over the past few years? If so, it is likely you have already experienced this book with different character names.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27827203.Frostblood__Frostblood_Saga___1_" title="Frostblood (Frostblood Saga, #1) by Elly Blake" rel="nofollow noopener">Frostblood</a> is just so... <b>unremarkable</b>. Everything about it is familiar and predictable, leading to a read that offered up no excitement, no need to keep turning the pages. It often feels as if YA fantasy publishers deliberately go looking for new authors to retell the same old recycled plots. Stick an attractive cover on the front and lets see if we can fool people into buying the same book over and over again.<br /><br />This book follows the heroine - Ruby - who is a Fireblood in a world where Frostbloods are the ruling class. Once again, this world is split evenly into two societal groups - an overdone technique that I find particularly lazy. It's the same with the Reds and Silvers in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22328546.Red_Queen__Red_Queen___1_" title="Red Queen (Red Queen, #1) by Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Queen</a>, the Reds and Golds in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15839976.Red_Rising__Red_Rising___1_" title="Red Rising (Red Rising, #1) by Pierce Brown" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Rising</a>, and the Shotet and Thuvhe from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30117284.Carve_the_Mark__Carve_the_Mark___1_" title="Carve the Mark (Carve the Mark, #1) by Veronica Roth" rel="nofollow noopener">Carve the Mark</a>, as well as others. <i>If only</i> the world were that simple! <i>If only</i> there were just two groups of people with differences. There is just no depth or complexity to a "this vs. this" world.<br /><br />Also, Ruby was <b>uninteresting and bland</b>. I feel like I have nothing to remember her by and it was really difficult to become invested in her story and troubles. The book opens with her mother being murdered and Ruby being captured by Frostblood soldiers; incidentally, this opening is almost identical to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30117284.Carve_the_Mark__Carve_the_Mark___1_" title="Carve the Mark (Carve the Mark, #1) by Veronica Roth" rel="nofollow noopener">Carve the Mark</a>, where Akos' father is murdered by the Shotet before Akos, himself, is captured. There's nothing here I haven't read before.<br /><br />Then, of course, the plot takes a completely mindblowing turn when our standard heroine with elemental powers (easy way of adding some magic without having to think too much about a magic system) <b>teams up with a hot guy (Arcus) to get revenge on the royals who wronged her</b>. Is it just me or are you getting déjà vu as well?<br /><br />And I don't know why so many authors think there is anything interesting about pages and pages of training. It's mind-numbing. <br /><br />But wait! Just when you thought this was all looking familiar, Arcus reveals his... dum, dum, dum, DARK PAST! Yes, that's right. Arcus is a very boring, very typical love interest, with very unoriginal secrets. <br /><br />A lot of YA fantasy is tropey and contains all the same elements, that's true, so maybe you could say I'm being harsh. But this book's problem is not just a series of components that make it derivative - it also has a very <b>lackluster style</b>. The writing did nothing to draw me in; dramatic events came and went without being engaging. There can be slow parts in any book, but even the most dynamic chapters didn’t hold any fire for me.<br /><br />To add a tiny bit of credit where it's due: by far the most interesting aspect of this book was the exploration of how one can be blamed for the actions of others they are grouped with. For example, the actions of a few radicals, whether they be Firebloods, POC, Muslims or feminists, can be used to make sweeping (and false) generalizations about all the others in said group. This is interesting and rather appropriate right now. Too bad it got lost under everything else.<br /><br />To summarize: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27827203.Frostblood__Frostblood_Saga___1_" title="Frostblood (Frostblood Saga, #1) by Elly Blake" rel="nofollow noopener">Frostblood</a> and my review feel so very familiar. I long for something new and different in YA fantasy.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="6591185287643704000" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1879055694" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1879055694" />
    <a title="Khurram" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25493797-khurram"><img alt="Khurram" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1383996638p2/25493797.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1879055694?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khurram" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khurram" href="/user/show/25493797-khurram">Khurram</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1879055694" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10845892838137807031">This is a Awsome debut novel. It is excellent by any novels standards. I was recommended this as I really liked the Throne of Glass and the story the story telling is right on par with this great series. If you grew up with fairytales and love superheroes you will love this story.<br/><br/>Ruby is a Fireblood (meaning she can generate frie) in a land ruled by by Frostbloods (the ability to generate ice), this is more that enough to get her killed. Thought the basics of her power by her grandmother, she is</span>
  <span id="freeText10845892838137807031" style="display:none">This is a Awsome debut novel. It is excellent by any novels standards. I was recommended this as I really liked the Throne of Glass and the story the story telling is right on par with this great series. If you grew up with fairytales and love superheroes you will love this story.<br /><br />Ruby is a Fireblood (meaning she can generate frie) in a land ruled by by Frostbloods (the ability to generate ice), this is more that enough to get her killed. Thought the basics of her power by her grandmother, she is hidden away by her mother. However when her secret is discovered and cost her everything she holds dear, she is burning for one thing revenge. When an opportunity is presented to her, she is dubious of trusting her natural enemies as allies.<br /><br />This story has it all, well written, well paced, action, romance, and even great character development. I like that fact that the characters natural personalities match their powers Ruby is fire so hot tempered, where as Frostbloods are portrayed is emotionally cold as they are powerful. However the characters are not one dimensional the all develop through the story. Ruby is constantly second guessing herself, but when she makes a decision she is determined to see it through no matter the cost to herself. I really enjoyed this book, and can't wait for the next one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10845892838137807031" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1796591677" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1796591677" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1796591677?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1796591677" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1497691263212940069">Reading ‘‘Frostblood’’ was a lot like reading ‘‘Storm Siren’’ for me, in terms of experience.<br/><br/>And I’m not only referring to the fact that both struggled to hold my interest. The characters in them have powers similar to Elsa’s from ‘‘Frozen,’’ especially Ruby who very much wants to be the new Elsa.<br/><br/>Indeed, the real problem is that those powers may be impressive – I mean, come on, who associates power with trash? No one – but they’re not entertaining to read about. Maybe on TV, this story would hav</span>
  <span id="freeText1497691263212940069" style="display:none">Reading ‘‘Frostblood’’ was a lot like reading ‘‘Storm Siren’’ for me, in terms of experience.<br /><br />And I’m not only referring to the fact that both struggled to hold my interest. The characters in them have powers similar to Elsa’s from ‘‘Frozen,’’ especially Ruby who very much wants to be the new Elsa.<br /><br />Indeed, the real problem is that those powers may be impressive – I mean, come on, who associates power with trash? No one – but they’re not entertaining to read about. Maybe on TV, this story would have engaged my interest a little more, but on paper the powers are not in 3-D, if you follow me.<br /><br />Plus, really, how many times have you heard this premise: hero/heroine is wronged by royally, therefore, he/she concocts a plan to kill or overthrown them? And that’s all they can think about: revenge.<br /><br />Do I see some hands raising? <br /><br />Nothing new. I’m actually feeling a bit unpatriotic right now, seeing that Elly Blake is Canadian and we all know that most books are written by American authors, so I felt quite proud of this lady for publishing a fantasy novel that seemed absolutely stupendous.<br /><br />But it’s not impressive, sadly. Even the writing has nothing new to offer. And I just really dislike how the blurb makes this big fuss about a certain ‘‘competition’’ between frostbloods and firebloods because, as you’ll see if you end up reading the book, it really isn’t a huge scene in the story.<br /><br />And the romance, bleh bleh bleh. I’m trying here… to find something positive to say about this book, and maybe the only thing I could say about it, something that can be said about most YA fantasy novels, is that this MAY appeal to you, if you have little to no experience with these types of novels. Sounds familiar? I must have mentioned this in dozens of my other negative reviews of YA fantasy novels.<br /><br />I’ll just watch Frozen now. If ‘‘Frostblood’’ is good for something, it’s to give you the irresistible need to play that movie.<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1497691263212940069" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1883988791" />
    <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin"><img alt="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603831478p2/17438949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1883988791" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14836305567410062466">Fire Meets Frost! <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484826829ra/21757200.gif' alt=' ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Ruby is a fireblood that her mother has tried to keep hidden because firebloods are being killed out by the frostbloods, at least the evil ones. She's very powerful but can't control her power as no one has trained her . . . until<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484826829ra/21757201.gif' alt=' ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Arcus is a frostblood and he's also very powerful. He is also something else that I can't tell you about, you have to read the book. He saves Ruby from a prison she was taken to when they evil ones found her. They killed her mother, she wants King Rasm</span>
  <span id="freeText14836305567410062466" style="display:none">Fire Meets Frost! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484826829ra/21757200.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ruby is a fireblood that her mother has tried to keep hidden because firebloods are being killed out by the frostbloods, at least the evil ones. She's very powerful but can't control her power as no one has trained her . . . until<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484826829ra/21757201.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Arcus is a frostblood and he's also very powerful. He is also something else that I can't tell you about, you have to read the book. He saves Ruby from a prison she was taken to when they evil ones found her. They killed her mother, she wants King Rasmus to die! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1474822688ra/20644856.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Arcus takes Ruby back to the Abbey where she meets some wonderful people. One being Brother Thistle. They want to train her to use her fire and control it. Brother Thistle and Arcus have their work cut out for them but it mostly works out in the end. They want to help her be able to take down King Rasmus. <br><br>Until Ruby is captured by the King's minions and brought back to his castle to fight in his pits. She is set up against people, animals, frostblood's. She hopes to be able to kill the king but will her plan every come into play? Maybe, maybe not, there is something else about the king . . . he's not quite right. Will Ruby with the help of Arcus be able to defeat the darkness. You shall see, when you read it! <br><br>I enjoyed the book. I love Arcus, he's my frost king =) There were a few things in the book that made me want to smack Ruby but it was still good. Sometimes it seemed like she could have used her powers before getting caught. Either way, it worked out good enough for me. <br><br>I will leave you with a funny little EXCERPT:<br><br><b>
  <i>"How did you find me?"<br><br>He unclenched his jaw to answer. " When Wheatgerm returned to the stables, I followed her tracks until they disappeared. And then I heard someone bellowing nonsense, and I knew it must be you."<br><br>"Who the blazes is Wheatgerm?" <br><br>"The horse you stole from the abbey," he said as if talking to a simpleton. <br><br>"You mean Butter. And I didn't steal her. I borrowed her. I take it she's safe?"<br><br>"Cold and tired, but safe in the stables eating like she's half starved. Which she probably is, thanks to you. And her name isn't Butter."<br><br>"It is now."<br><br>"She's not yours to name."<br><br>"She's mine in spirit now that we've had an adventure together. And her name suits her. She's soft and yellow, like butter." <br><br>He made a disgusted sound. "If we all had names to suit us, you'd be called Thorn in My Backside. Or Plague of the Gods."<br><br>I prickled at his scathing tone. "And you'd be Miserable Blockhead."<br><br>"Is that the best you could do?"<br><br>"Give me time. I'm half frozen."<i></i></i>
</b><br><br>I just love Ruby and Arcus! ❤<br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2017/01/frostblood-by-elly-blake.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>

<div id="review_1802760350" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1802760350" />
    <a title="Hailey (Hailey in Bookland)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21937982-hailey-hailey-in-bookland"><img alt="Hailey (Hailey in Bookland)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560365354p2/21937982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1802760350?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hailey (Hailey in Bookland)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hailey (Hailey in Bookland)" href="/user/show/21937982-hailey-hailey-in-bookland">Hailey (Hailey in Bookland)</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1917568641" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1917568641" />
    <a title="elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51318038-elena"><img alt="elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605725028p2/51318038.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1917568641?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="elena" href="/user/show/51318038-elena">elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1917568641" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10347677112945483645"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Stillness was a kind of violence in the hands of people who played at handing out pain.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>This was the typical YA fantasy book that you see everywhere else. It's got similar plot twists, similar heroine's and hero's, the typical romance, the action that is set somewhere, the similar settings - it's all similar - <b>but it's also something I don't get tired of.</b> Elly Blake actually managed to make me <b>laugh, smile, scream inside, and basically cover my mouth</b> as the ending was coming because i</span>
  <span id="freeText10347677112945483645" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Stillness was a kind of violence in the hands of people who played at handing out pain.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />This was the typical YA fantasy book that you see everywhere else. It's got similar plot twists, similar heroine's and hero's, the typical romance, the action that is set somewhere, the similar settings - it's all similar - <b>but it's also something I don't get tired of.</b> Elly Blake actually managed to make me <b>laugh, smile, scream inside, and basically cover my mouth</b> as the ending was coming because it was something I didn't expect.<br /><br /><i>Frostblood</i> is about Ruby, a 17-year-old who is a Fireblood living in a world of Frostbloods so just by knowing that, the reader knows that Ruby doesn't get along with her people because they are either different than her, are her enemies, or are afraid of her powers. One day, soldiers come looking for this Fireblood to kill her because they want to get rid of Fireblood's as soon as they can - since it's been happening for quite some time now and there are really no Fireblood's left - and once they find Ruby and her mother, Ruby knows she has to do something to run away. Because Ruby doesn't know how to use her gift, how to control her fire abilities, her mother ends up defending her when a soldier was about to kill her and ends up dying, leaving Ruby alone and is taken away to a prison cell. Days later, 2 strangers arrive where Ruby is and offer her something she doesn't think she could regret: <b>kill the Frost King and she will earn freedom.</b> Hearing the word <i>freedom</i> is all Ruby could think about, so she agrees to do the task she is offered, but the thing is, she doesn't know <b>what her task is and doesn't really realize what she just got herself into until seeing it.</b> Arcus, one of the people who carried her out to escape and be taken away to train doesn't see her as anything but dangerous and is tired of having to <b>need</b> because he believes in what they have told him: <b>that the Fireblood is the key to peace.</b> <br /><br />Ruby begins training at this different place with people that are nothing like her and little did she know that she would be able to trust some of these people, and even fall in love with the "icy young man." As she begins this train, Ruby is actually taken away to another cell but instead of staying there suffering, she is forced to fight and battle in the pit of the Frostblood King <b>against</b> Frostbloods when she is a Fireblood. Ruby, being forced to become stronger than she thought she was, starts gaining this powerful strength delivered from the light (or darkness) and doesn't realize what she can do until after. This might just be her chance to complete the task and kill the ruthless ruler and get revenge and what he has done to her.<br /><br />Frostblood wasn't new. Like I said, it was the typical YA fantasy that has sights of romance and a new ship that may or may not sink which is making me scream inside because I ended up shipping Arcus and Ruby. The fantasy elements are the same ones you would see in other books, like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22328546.Red_Queen__Red_Queen___1_" title="Red Queen (Red Queen, #1) by Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener"> Red Queen</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17399160.Snow_Like_Ashes__Snow_Like_Ashes___1_" title="Snow Like Ashes (Snow Like Ashes, #1) by Sara Raasch" rel="nofollow noopener"> Snow like Ashes</a>. I admit I don't get tired of it. I understand the hate an author can get because readers think they are basically copying another work of another author and making it theirs in ways, changing the plot, the world-building, the characters, the fantasy elements - changing everything - but then, I really don't care. I'm here reading a book and I'm entertained. I like it, I finish it, and maybe I'll cry.<br /><br /><b>But I didn't hate Frostblood, I merely enjoyed it.</b><br /><br />The characters were okay. The world-building was okay. Everything was okay. In fantasy books, I can never relate to characters and see where they're coming from, and Ruby was no different. She was the typical heroine that has a gift she doesn't know how to use unless she gets trained. Arcus was the typical hero in the story that has a secret past (dark or not) that reveals it later but to be honest, it's kind of obvious in Part 1 of the story. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[There are lines where he is named "god" and I knew from that instant that he was the lost King and not his brother. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Ruby was quite boring, I admit, but at least she managed to fight well enough to survive and live, and to become the champion of the king! The typical things we see in YA fantasy novels like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7896527.Throne_of_Glass__Throne_of_Glass___1_" title="Throne of Glass (Throne of Glass, #1) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener"> Throne of Glass</a>. Her abilities improved, which reminded me of Mare from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22328546.Red_Queen__Red_Queen___1_" title="Red Queen (Red Queen, #1) by Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener"> Red Queen</a> and I was quite happy she did because she was really boring at first that I couldn't really care about her. Ruby wasn't that strong, but she managed to survive in the battle and she even made history <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[by becoming the first Fireblood to defeat a Frostblood. <b>Hooray!</b> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />When I come to think of it, 2 stars is what this deserves from me. I kind of agree with Emily May and her review, where you see such similarities when you're reading this and all you get are vibes from other books. I'm not the biggest fan of fantasy myself, but this was quite bland and <b>unoriginal.</b> Arcus has his dark past/secret past that he reveals in the end and it wasn't surprising. I've said this quite some times now, <b>but I am not the kind of person that will predict something when it comes to a book.</b> I try my best to not think about what will happen next because I want to find out (which is the point of reading) but in Frostblood, it was so obvious. <br /><br />Arcus now, was someone I ended up loving when I hated him at first. I hated his attitude in the beginning and did not agree with the way he would treat Ruby, but then he managed to change a little <b>because she changed him in ways.</b> Yes, they are cute together, and I was so happy to read moments of them together after they shared their kiss, but it wasn't surprising where I was just left shocked and/or surprised. I was just rooting for them and was hoping they would end up together. Arcus was the typical aggressive hero in books, <b>which is the type I like, depending on how they are</b> and I can see why he was an "asshole" to Ruby at first. <b>I loved how he was a warrior and he acted like one, he spoke like a nobleman, he would fight when he needed to, and he was there for his people, including Ruby, when he knew they needed him.</b> He would also care for his people and would treat them with such care and I just loved that so much. I loved him, <b>I really did,</b> I just hated him in the beginning because he was so harsh with Ruby when she was just learning about her gift; how to use it, how to control it. Of course, his character grew on me and although I didn't swoon, the way he would act around Ruby and smile or grin was just so cute and it always made me smile.<br /><br />Arcus was one of the characters that I can spend all day talking about how much I love him. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[He started crying when his brother died but thanked Ruby for that and I was just weak; <i>left weak!!</i> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I want him and Ruby to be together throughout the whole trilogy and it makes me sad because I sense a love triangle in the second book and I really don't want that. I don't want Ruby to go for another guy when it might just be her worst choice when she already has <b>the perfect guy there, loving her and caring for her and waiting for her</b>. He's a dark warrior who trained her and fell for her and basically offered his life for her after he makes sure she is safe in the city. <i>What more could Ruby <u>possibly</u> want??</i> Arcus is precious, strong, and I love him. He changed for the best and he's weak when it comes to Ruby and I love that. I admit I don't rate books with half stars, <b>but this book deserves 2 1/2 stars because I've come to the point where I realize that I love Arcus despite the hate I had for him in the beginning.</b> I just need more Arcus and Ruby moments and if Blake doesn't give me that, I will be very disappointed and I will be a ranty bitch about it in my review for the second book.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Also, there's finally a book where there is a lost king and I'm sure there are much more but I have not read them! There's always a lost princess or queen, a lost rightful ruler that was seen to be dead or killed, and it was the same with Arcus, but he was the lost king. <b>ARCUS IS ARELIUS ARKANUS, SON OF AKUR, ELDER BROTHER TO RASMUS (THE CURRENT FROST KING THAT RUBY MANAGED TO KILL IN FRONT OF HIS BROTHER WHICH WAS SAD BUT SHE HAD TO) AND I DONT KNOW HOW IT WILL BE FOR HIM TO RECLAIM HIS THRONE BUT I WAS HAPPY WHEN I FOUND OUT</b> (actually I predicted it which is why this lost a star; for being too predictable). IF RUBY DOESNT BECOME THE FROSTBLOOD QUEEN OR SOMETHING I WILL SUE AND THROW MY BOOK EVERYWHERE.<br /><br /><blockquote><i><b>I come to you as Arelius Arkanus, son of Akur, elder brother to Rasmus. I was burned by an assassin and left for dead. But I did not die.</b></i></blockquote> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Now back to things that I didn't like</b> - Ruby's power was also weak, and I was upset how she couldn't become stronger before <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[becoming the champion of the King. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> The way she trained and tried was just boring, bland, dull, and she was just a boring character in general. I'm probably complaining too much about her, but it's true. I wish she was able to control it more and was able to gain more strength <b>from her training.</b> When it came to her mother's death, I expected her to literally become a ball of flames or just explode into fire or something and kill soldiers. The book started off with her practicing her powers so I thought she would know something, or a little more than what she already knew, so like in other novels, I thought she was gonna get strength <b>from seeing her dead mother; the one who gave her strength and accepted her no matter who she was</b> but instead, she was just so weak. You know those books where the hero or heroine cry so hard because they are seeing a loved one die, just fall away, and as they are crying out tears, they get strength from it? Like they're seeing this person die in their arms, they're seeing this important person fade away and they know they will never see them again, and suddenly they just <b>explode</b> because they are taking something or someone so special from their life so they let out all of their anger and everything just...<b>EXPLODES!?!</b> Well, I expected that from Ruby. <br /><br /><b>But I didn't get it.</b><br /><br />Instead, she was taken away and was locked up in that prison cell that she managed to survive. <br /><br />The plot twist was not surprising. It was predictable, which like I said, is something I usually don't get, but it was there. The world-building was also <i>okay.</i> The plot twist can be seen since Arcus reveals some of his personality. He was called <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[a god by a Brother and when Ruby asked about his patience, a Brother would answer that that is the patience of a God, so I figured he was the God of the North or some kind of King. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I was actually glad he was secretly falling for Ruby and the nicknames he had for her were just so cute, like his little inferno, but I just wasn't satisfied with everything. There isn't really much romance until around 100 pages, which I was completely fine with because that is completely normal in pretty much all books that have romance in it. Frostblood is the kind of novel that has 2 main characters that <b>go from enemies to lovers</b> and I loved that. I love the kind of books that form a well-developed relationship like that, and this didn't fail to do that. No matter how long it takes, I am here for that ship, and I will live for that ship. I also recommend not reading the description for the second book because there are <b>minor spoilers</b> from this book.<br /><br />Another thing I <b>did enjoy</b> was how the Brother's had patience with Ruby. They were supportive of her and believed in her, unlike Arcus in the beginning, and I was happy about that. I was happy she had people <b>by her side and I was happy she was able to call them friends</b>. Even if they weren't considered friends, they felt like friends when they were together. Reading those chapters made me happy because Ruby realized a lot of things about her that she didn't know. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<b>She's either a healer like her mother or she's the daughter of darkness.</b><br /><br />Honestly, I think she's the daughter of darkness because the third book - since this is supposed to be a trilogy I guess - is called "Darkblood" so I guess she will go from a Frostblood to a Fireblood to a Darkblood. I mean, doesn't the title give it all away? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Overall, <i>Frostblood</i> was an okay book. I was debating whether or not this book deserves 2 or 3 stars, but I skimmed some pages and I hated most of the beginning; Ruby wasn't an interesting character and she wasn't the kind of heroine that I enjoy reading about; It took me a while to get used to Arcus' character only to completely fall in love with him. I did say I laughed - Elly blake did manage to make me laugh - but it was Arcus' attitude toward Ruby (although I felt bad). If you're just starting to read YA Fantasy, this would be a good start. If you enjoyed <i>Red Queen</i>. I'm sure you'll enjoy this one. If you didn't, I would still recommend it because I have some friends who enjoyed this one and completely disliked <i>Red Queen by Victoria Aveyard.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="10347677112945483645" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Ahmed  Ejaz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53694260-ahmed-ejaz"><img alt="Ahmed  Ejaz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598778737p2/53694260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1932237430?book_show_action=true">Mar 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ahmed  Ejaz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ahmed  Ejaz" href="/user/show/53694260-ahmed-ejaz">Ahmed  Ejaz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53694260-ahmed-ejaz?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53694260-ahmed-ejaz?shelf=full-lengths">full-lengths</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1932237430" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15985941676831935672"><blockquote> <b> <i> A focused mind is a powerful tool </i></b>
</blockquote> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489072283ra/22182981.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><i>Frostblood</i> is one of the books which I enjoyed the most. After Red Queen, I was wanting more on blood discrimination. And few days ago I found this piece of writing which I will never forget.<br/>The most important thing I liked in this book is its way of writing. It is just beyond amazing. At least for me. I enjoyed reading how author expressed things. How she made me smile by some jokes in conversations, made me excited by the action scenes, made me sad by so</span>
  <span id="freeText15985941676831935672" style="display:none"><blockquote> <b> <i> A focused mind is a powerful tool </i></b>
</blockquote> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489072283ra/22182981.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><i>Frostblood</i> is one of the books which I enjoyed the most. After Red Queen, I was wanting more on blood discrimination. And few days ago I found this piece of writing which I will never forget.<br>The most important thing I liked in this book is its way of writing. It is just beyond amazing. At least for me. I enjoyed reading how author expressed things. How she made me smile by some jokes in conversations, made me excited by the action scenes, made me sad by some scenes. In short this is one of the best writing styles I have ever read. <br><br><br><b>
  <u>OVERVIEW</u>
</b><br>Ruby is a Fireblood, the kind which is not acceptable in the kingdom where the Frost King, Rasmus, rules. Her mother is killed in an attack by the Soldiers of Frost King. In the attack, Ruby is imprisoned by them. But she gets free by the rebels who wants to remove Rasmus from power. They are planning to use Ruby for their purpose. But Ruby has her purpose also. Revenge. Revenge of her mother's death.<br>The he very big surprise is rebels are also the Frostbloods. They are doing this for a reason.<br>Rasmus, Frost King, hates Firebloods for a reason. That's why he kills them. <br><br><b>
  <u> THINGS I LIKED</u>
</b><br>=&gt;Discrimination, I liked how the world is divided in Firebloods and Frostbloods. <br><br>=&gt;Arcus, this character is just amazing. My favourite male character after Paxton (from Great Hunt). He was just a mystery till the end of the book. The book revealed his mystery in a very well manner. I liked the way his character was written. Even though I found him rude in the beginning but eventually I came to know why he was rude.<br><br>=&gt;Arena Scenes, those were very well written. I was literally feeling that I was watching these scenes. I was Feeling the atmosphere of arena. <br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br><br>=&gt;Death Scene of Captain (killer of Ruby's mother), Ruby was giving him the chance to save his life. She became soft-hearted because of his daughter and wife were in the arena even though he didn't deserve mercy. But Captain, out of pride, didn't listen. <br><br>=&gt;Entry of Arcus in Arena, whoa! I couldn't believe what I was reading when this scene came. I was just stunned. But equally feeling good. <br><br>=&gt;Relationship of Arcus and Ruby, that was nice. I liked them being together. But when the Rasmus came, I got afraid. I was thinking that Ruby might begin to love him. But thank God that didn't came. Otherwise I wouldn't have liked it. Because I had already liked the Arcus and Ruby. I wouldn't have liked Rasmus in between. <br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><blockquote> <b> <i> Those who can’t control themselves will find themselves under the control of others </i></b>
</blockquote><br><b>
  <u>RANDOM THOUGHTS</u>
</b><br>This book is divided into two parts. Some people may get bored by the first part. But I didn't. Even though that was little boring. This is the beauty of this book. Even in little boring scenes, author keeps giving us little bits which keep us curious. Regardless, I enjoyed both parts equally. <br><br><br>After reading this book, I have found my new favourite author. Elly Blake. I will be looking forward to more books from her. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> Weapons and hot tempers make a dangerous pair </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>March 9, 2017</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2906678035" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer12066898444261590347"><b>DNF @ 37%</b><br/><br/>I don't usually rate books I DNF unless I make it to 50%, but this book has me bitter...even though it's pretty much my fault. Still. I got drawn into the hype and pretty cover and so, I bought not only <i>this</i> book in hardcover...but also books two and three...Because IDIOT. Regardless, you can imagine how much I wanted to love and persevere through this thing and its successors. <br/><br/>But alas, as much as I loathe wasting money, I just can't force myself to pick this book up anymore. <br/><br/>It basica</span>
  <span id="freeText12066898444261590347" style="display:none"><b>DNF @ 37%</b><br /><br />I don't usually rate books I DNF unless I make it to 50%, but this book has me bitter...even though it's pretty much my fault. Still. I got drawn into the hype and pretty cover and so, I bought not only <i>this</i> book in hardcover...but also books two and three...Because IDIOT. Regardless, you can imagine how much I wanted to love and persevere through this thing and its successors. <br /><br />But alas, as much as I loathe wasting money, I just can't force myself to pick this book up anymore. <br /><br />It basically reads like every other YA fantasy romance you've ever read before, except SHITTY. I have read (and rated highly) many a cliched YA in my time, but this one just isn't cutting the mustard. The writing is blah, the characters are wooden and one-dimensional, and the magic system is non-existent. <br /><br />The only silver lining here is that I get to pare down my physical tbr by three books, albeit not via the avenue I would prefer. Thankfully though, I have since trained myself to stop buying entire series at once without first reading and loving book one. I still have a few unread series on my shelves which were purchased before said training took place, but hopefully I have better luck with those. <br /><br />Onward.</span>

<div id="review_1795342793" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1795342793" />
    <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please"><img alt="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570038444p2/8422853.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1795342793?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=my-favorite-covers">my-favorite-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=arc-physical-pusblisher">arc-physical-pusblisher</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=could-read-over-and-over-again">could-read-over-and-over-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=in-the-minority-on-this-one">in-the-minority-on-this-one</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=unforgettable-male-leads">unforgettable-male-leads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1795342793" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8511880950689368524"><i>**As promised, here is the <i>Frostblood</i> giveaway (and more!) on our blog-sponsored by Little, Brown!! <b>Click <a href='http://starcrossedbookblog.com/2017/02/book-reviewgiveaway-frostblood-frostblood-saga-1-by-elly-blake/' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a> to enter!</b> **</i><br/><br/><i>Frostblood</i> is one of those books that you see and you know you just <i>have</i> to read it. If not from the cover alone (umm, hello pretty cover), then by the promising synopsis. I first saw this book back in early winter-it popped up out of nowhere and stole my heart before I even read it. <b>It was a case of love at first sight</b>, and I knew nothing would do until I had this book in m</span>
  <span id="freeText8511880950689368524" style="display:none"><i>**As promised, here is the <i>Frostblood</i> giveaway (and more!) on our blog-sponsored by Little, Brown!! <b>Click <a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/2017/02/book-reviewgiveaway-frostblood-frostblood-saga-1-by-elly-blake/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> to enter!</b> **</i><br><br><i>Frostblood</i> is one of those books that you see and you know you just <i>have</i> to read it. If not from the cover alone (umm, hello pretty cover), then by the promising synopsis. I first saw this book back in early winter-it popped up out of nowhere and stole my heart before I even read it. <b>It was a case of love at first sight</b>, and I knew nothing would do until I had this book in my hands. <br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/tumblr_inline_o9smqerosb1rk03if_500_zps58ivu5rv.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1486138631ra/21885698.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_inline_o9smqerosb1rk03if_500_zps58ivu5rv.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And, finally, riiiiight before it was about to come out, I got the opportunity from Little, Brown to receive a (again, GORGEOUS) finished copy to enjoy. And enjoy I did. <b>There wasn’t one moment where I wasn’t fully engrossed in this story</b>. From page one on, I was hooked. I honestly am just the easiest person to please with YA fantasy-<b>give me a young tortured male with a heart made of ice</b> (pretty much literally and figuratively), a hate-hate relationship…<b>and I. Am. SOLD.</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“She’s not yours to name.”<br>“She’s mine in spirit now that we’ve had an adventure together. And her name suits her. She’s soft and yellow, like butter.”<br>He made a disgusted sound. “If we all had names to suit us, you’d be called Thorn in My Backside. Or Plague of the Gods.”<br>I prickled at his scathing tone. “And you’d be Miserable Blockhead.”<br>“Is that the best you can do?”<br>“Give me time. I’m half frozen.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/6857824_zpsc5vmdkse.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1486138554ra/21885692.gif" alt=" photo 6857824_zpsc5vmdkse.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This book was clearly no exception. The first chapter broke my heart immediately-I mean <i>whyyyyy</i>-making it clear from the start that the author didn’t mind getting her hands dirty. I like that. I like that a LOT, and, even more than that, <b>I respect it immensely</b>. <br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/13548769_zpsonjdpdvw.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1486138631ra/21885699.gif" alt=" photo 13548769_zpsonjdpdvw.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I’m not above setting a heavy precedent-it gives a book fire, passion, a reason to fight-and I’ve always loved that. Ruby is a Fireblood, a hunted people that can produce, you guessed it, <i>fire</i>, and who are immensely hot to the touch. Hunted by Frostbloods, the rare Firebloods who have not been found (and executed or sent to compete for sure death) yet are forced to hide, to keep themselves scarce. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“You speak as if I’m as heavy as an ox,” I said. “Last week I was a bundle of sticks.”<br>“You’re still too thin.”<br>“Perhaps if I gain some weight, you won’t call me a stick anymore.”<br>“You may hope to one day be a branch.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Ruby is in hiding with her mother in a village, not able to practice her craft or live freely as she’d hope. One thing leads to another, and Ruby is saved from a certain death after being captured by the Frostblood king’s guard...by none other than Frostblood rebels-the infuriating Arcus being one of them.<br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/682410_zpsfmvn4o2i.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1486138691ra/21885712.gif" alt=" photo 682410_zpsfmvn4o2i.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I must say, <b>I ADORED Arcus</b>. He was moody, wounded, but loyal to all those around him and Ruby’s biggest ally. Well…eventually…but he was always a driving force in helping her train, in helping her become the best she could be. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“And my touch threatens that somehow?”<br>“In a way. I brought you here to prepare you for a huge task,” he said, dipping the cloth in the water and touching it to my cheek again. “An enormous weight rests on your shoulders.”<br>I sighed, irritated at the reminder of what made me truly important. I wanted to mean more to Arcus than a way to melt the throne. <br>"And now I wonder if I can let you go,” he added quietly. </blockquote>
</b><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/7_zpsf1binm9m.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1486138554ra/21885693.gif" alt=" photo 7_zpsf1binm9m.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>After seeing who Ruby is, how fiercely she wants to help, <b>he starts to [secretly] fall for her</b>, starts doing everything in his power to change what the rebel group wants from Ruby, to find literally any other way….because their plan leads to nothing but suicide. <br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/cd9bd2e9e39743729ed3ad66455a2687_zps3m92ednu.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1486138554ra/21885694.gif" alt=" photo cd9bd2e9e39743729ed3ad66455a2687_zps3m92ednu.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I just <b>loved how antagonistic these two were towards each other</b> and how they slowly began to find solace in one another-it was sweet, <b>slow-burning</b>, and the way he wanted to protect her, even when he didn’t like her, melted my [not so] icy little heart. And the fact that the rebel plan included him not leaving her side? Come on. Just…come on, *sighs* I lubbs him. I really do.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“Who else is there?” He asked. “What Fireblood will do this but you?”<br>“What if I destroy the throne? When it’s all over, are you just going to”-I waved a hand-“disappear into the air like mist?”<br>“From the time we leave the abbey until you’re safely back again, I’ll protect you with my life.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>So, you know, once again I feel like I’m out on a limb here, by myself, loving a book that’s absolutely wonderful all by myself. I don’t get it!!! <b>What isn’t to like??</b> Swoony boy. Loyal boy. <i>Fierce</i> boy. Fierce girl. Mortal enemies. Enemies-to-lovers. Perilistic ending. <b>Tons of [male] </b>(male male male-NEED ANY MORE HINTS?) <b>sacrifice</b>. Tons of win. You people are crazy…but that’s okay. This book is wonderful-and I will proudly display this beauty on my shelf forever.<br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea-peril-please-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452287303i/17673713._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a title="Facebook" href="https://www.facebook.com/starcrossedbookblog" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055977i/15660595.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<div id="review_1625767206" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1625767206" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1625767206?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebekah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebekah" href="/user/show/2669249-rebekah">Rebekah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2669249-rebekah?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2669249-rebekah?shelf=ya-addiction">ya-addiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2669249-rebekah?shelf=must-own">must-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2669249-rebekah?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2669249-rebekah?shelf=clean">clean</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1625767206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1999029358104258415">This book was FREAKING AWESOME!!! A MUST OWN! A book that has all the elements for an amazing book! A book you would lose sleep over because you can't put it down! A book you find yourself gripping to find out what happens and the anticipation of the action in this book!<br/><p>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1485893830ra/21858946.gif' alt='3ornjxiishz2mgyyhu' width='500' height='281' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</p><br/><p><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1485893831i/21858947.jpg' alt='64eacd7c2d6bc5ca1c378df03194b7e4.jpg' width='201' height='146' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>Alright, so this book is about Frostbloods and Firebloods. Firebloods are hot and have control over fire in this book we do however have some <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1485893831i/21858948._SY540_.jpg' alt='46fba53f9553d275f923bad26ef75c6f.jpg' width='165' height='248' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>people who have n</p></span>
  <span id="freeText1999029358104258415" style="display:none">This book was FREAKING AWESOME!!! A MUST OWN! A book that has all the elements for an amazing book! A book you would lose sleep over because you can't put it down! A book you find yourself gripping to find out what happens and the anticipation of the action in this book!<br><p>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1485893830ra/21858946.gif" alt="3ornjxiishz2mgyyhu" width="500" height="281" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><br><p><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1485893831i/21858947.jpg" alt="64eacd7c2d6bc5ca1c378df03194b7e4.jpg" width="201" height="146" class="gr-hostedUserImg">Alright, so this book is about Frostbloods and Firebloods. Frostbloods are people who can control ice and snow and are cold. Firebloods are hot and have control over fire in this book we do however have some <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1485893831i/21858948._SY540_.jpg" alt="46fba53f9553d275f923bad26ef75c6f.jpg" width="165" height="248" class="gr-hostedUserImg">people who have neither. The world building isn't anything new where the Frostbloods rule and are trying to exterminate the Firebloods. There is a lot of legends, myths, history when it comes to these people and I enjoyed exploring that and learning more about it throughout the story.</p><br><p><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1485893831i/21858949._SY540_.jpg" alt="58b62e03cfe348820e35972caddf8366.jpg" width="337" height="337" class="gr-hostedUserImg">Because of this Ruby has suppressed her power of fire all her seventeen years of life. In secret and behind her mother's back she feels like she should somehow practice. Her Grandmother, before she died was trying to teach her how to control it but now her mother didn't want it to manifest at all otherwise she should be caught and put to death. I REALLY liked Ruby, she has a temper and a lack of controlling it, she lets her emotions run wild, she is feisty, fierce, strong, yet good and kind. I REALLY enjoyed everything about her character even her raging sack of hormones.</p><br><p>Then we have Arcus, I loved everything about him. So swoon-worthy in every way. He is <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1485893831i/21858950._SY540_.jpg" alt="5c3aceff2142026f41dcace98fa51b0a.jpg" width="232" height="304" class="gr-hostedUserImg">NOT your typical swoon worthy male character and I LOVE THAT! He constantly wears a hood, he is SUPER strong and good at his control over his powers of frost and tries to help Ruby with her powers and temper even though he has one as well...well when it comes to her that is.</p><br><p>I loved their relationship, they were enemies with a common purpose. I was a bit disappointed when I felt their relationship changed and developed almost too quickly but that is nothing against the book just something I prefer.</p><br><p>Overall: I absolutely loved everything about this book, it's fast paced, action packed, doesn't have a romance that overwhelms the story, it keeps you on your toes and you won't be able to put this down once you start it! AH! I loved it!</p><br><p>Sexual Content: mild<br>Violence: moderate<br>Language: none<br>Drugs/Alcohol: none</p><br><p>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1485893831i/21858951._SY540_.jpg" alt="own" width="292" height="292" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1485893547i/21858924.jpg" alt="bekah" width="369" height="134" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><br><p>
  <strong>*A HUGE thank you to Little, Brown Books for Young Readers for this ARC which I got in exchange for an honest review*</strong>

<div id="review_1832207102" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1832207102" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1832207102?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1832207102" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14054269508586612846"><i>Frostblood</i> was nothing special per se, but that doesn't make this a bad book. If you enjoyed <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1029695521' rel='nofollow noopener'>Throne of Glass</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1333450240' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Queen of the Tearling</a>, and/or <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1342927423' rel='nofollow noopener'> Snow Like Ashes </a> then you will probably really enjoy this book. And you know what star rating I gave all of those books I just listed? <b>Three stars</b>, too. Strong, young female protagonist, who got dealt a bad hand in their early life, is now fighting for their rightful place on the throne. This story-line isn't bad, but it is not anything new or groundbre</span>
  <span id="freeText14054269508586612846" style="display:none"><i>Frostblood</i> was nothing special per se, but that doesn't make this a bad book. If you enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1029695521" rel="nofollow noopener">Throne of Glass</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1333450240" rel="nofollow noopener">The Queen of the Tearling</a>, and/or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1342927423" rel="nofollow noopener"> Snow Like Ashes </a> then you will probably really enjoy this book. And you know what star rating I gave all of those books I just listed? <b>Three stars</b>, too. Strong, young female protagonist, who got dealt a bad hand in their early life, is now fighting for their rightful place on the throne. This story-line isn't bad, but it is not anything new or groundbreaking that is going to change YA fantasy as we know it. And there isn't anything wrong with that, either, but it also isn't going to get five stars or make any best of 2017 lists, for me.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484188525ra/21691525.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The magic in this world is separated from people that wield frost, Frostbloods, and people that wield fire, Firebloods. Which, by the way, the book for sure emphasizes a Fireblood, and how needed she was, so I feel like <i>this</i> book should have been titled Fireblood, and perhaps the next be Frostblood. But I don't work in the publishing world, so who am I? Anyways, Frostbloods show extreme prejudice towards Firebloods, to the point that they seem pretty much extinct. The kingdom in this world is ruled by the Frost King, and his whole arsenal is frost users. When they discover Firebloods, they capture them, treat them horribly, and then force them to compete for their lives in an arena versus a Frostblood Champion, which the Fireblood will always die. That is, until the most powerful Fireblood ever to be born is found. <i>*dun dun duuun*</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/486663.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ruby, said powerful Fireblood, is only seventeen, and dealing with the very new loss of her mother. After escaping prison, she finds herself at the mercy of some Frostblood monks, who are trying to teach her the full potential of her power. One of those monks is name Arcus, and I was actually a fan of him. Both of his "plot-twists" were incredibly predictable, but I actually did like him as a character. He was probably the shining light of this story for me. Hell, maybe I'm happy the book was called <i>Frostblood</i>, because he was my favorite. <br><br>I do fear for his story-line, though, because (not to get into spoiler territory) he has a disfigurement, and I feel like the author walked that line of sympathy and "I wish he was normal" and I was scared that I was going to have to give this book one star on quite a few occasions, but she never crossed that line. I loved that Arcus wasn't perfect, and I loved his imperfection; I just hope Ruby keeps loving it, too. <br><br>There is a good discussion in this book about how we perceive others, and marginalize the group in which they are in, off of what other people say about them/the group. Obviously this is something pretty important and relevant in 2017, and anything that is able to start a discussion and have others start to think about this important topic is absolutely amazing. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484188525ra/21691526.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is Elly Blake's debut novel, and I think she does have potential to develop this story into something that I will think is above average. Like I said, I didn't dislike this book by any stretch of the imagination; I just wanted more than what I received. I will for sure continue on with book two, and I will definitely give this world and these characters another chance. <br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany/profile" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="14054269508586612846" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1932196721" />
    <a title="sreeja" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50309540-sreeja"><img alt="sreeja" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598363186p2/50309540.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1932196721?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="sreeja" class="user" itemprop="url" name="sreeja" href="/user/show/50309540-sreeja">sreeja</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781473635173" href="/book/show/31134210-frostblood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50309540-sreeja?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>,

          </div>
