        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1932196721" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2365540116065323579"><b> “Stillness was a kind of violence in the hands of people who played at handing out pain.” </b><br/> 2.5★<br/>First off let me just start by saying that I did <i>not</i> HATE this book per se; I was just really disappointed by how it turned out and the cliché events that took place. Frostblood follows Ruby who is a Fireblood living in Fors; which is basically a place where she will be hunted down for her powers and what she can do. Along the book she finds her way grows as a character and does everything that is usu</span>
  <span id="freeText2365540116065323579" style="display:none"><b> “Stillness was a kind of violence in the hands of people who played at handing out pain.” </b><br> 2.5★<br>First off let me just start by saying that I did <i>not</i> HATE this book per se; I was just really disappointed by how it turned out and the cliché events that took place. Frostblood follows Ruby who is a Fireblood living in Fors; which is basically a place where she will be hunted down for her powers and what she can do. Along the book she finds her way grows as a character and does everything that is usually done in a typical YA book. <br><u>List of All the cliché things that happen in this book:</u> <br><i>Exhibit A</i>: <b>special snowflake</b> of a girl whose powers are the reason the world will be saved the girl however; doesn’t know this and when told she will probably be disbelieving and shocked and in denial<br><a href="http://s1064.photobucket.com/user/simplysreeja/media/06b9ffe7-8230-41ed-b12d-3014108d1709_zpsqr00roxr.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490974768i/22365357.png" alt=" photo 06b9ffe7-8230-41ed-b12d-3014108d1709_zpsqr00roxr.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>Exhibit B</i>: the main love interest and Ruby are polar opposites and absolutely <i>hate</i> each other at first before learning to love and accept each other. Now where have I seen this before??<br><a href="https://gifyu.com/image/SBhz" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490974768ra/22365358.gif" alt="23a7e2bd0d5142b24a03f62c86882bdc.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>Exhibit C</i>: a prophecy of any sort with the mc in it which leads to YES, you guessed it more denial and more “but why am I the chosen one” moments.<br><a href="https://gifyu.com/image/SBh9" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490974768ra/22365356.gif" alt="2002454c9ea1d1d33c7c28466372628d.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>Exhibit D</i>: the forcing of a completely unnecessary and really awkward love triangle (minor one) down the reader’s throats. LIKE PLS STOP.<br><a href="https://gifyu.com/image/SBhp" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490974768ra/22365355.gif" alt="cde396e6dfb46bfeb3065ea4f4b81ab6.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Honestly, I have a feeling there were more but I just can’t remember all the scenes and details so let me just get down to the actual story *cracks knuckles*. Oh boy, the plot felt extremely rushed and awkward at the first few chapters but the pacing starts to get better towards the middle and the end. I must say that the plot got a whole lot better towards the end and I was surprised by it. <br>The writing style is simple it’s not too over the top but some of the scenes were really boring. The characters were bearable and their development and character arc were quite alright. The plot itself was quite cliché but I did end up enjoying it towards the end because of how the story developed. In the end however, I felt no connection with the characters at all but maybe it will get better for me as the series goes on? The magical elements of this book was quite interesting though and the folklore and myths of their land was interesting to follow. <br>LOW POINTS:<br>a)	the pacing in the beginning<br>b)	that shitty love triangle <br>c)	basically all those tropes in general<br><br>HIGHLIGHTS:<br>a)	powers <br><a href="https://gifyu.com/image/SBhc" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491024491ra/22369351.gif" alt="1a53630b806604cc1e849b424cf2f552.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>b)	fight scenes<br>c)	Arcus <br><a href="https://gifyu.com/image/SBhi" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491024491ra/22369352.gif" alt="18a1f8fa76426b5d4dd3003828f023f5.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Overall, I would say that this book was alright and I might end up continuing the series to see if it gets better.</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=canadian-authors">canadian-authors</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1782565016" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17550627581982098099">An Advance Reader Copy was provided by the publisher for review. Quotes pulled from the ARC may be incorrect and may be subject to change.<br/><br/>Welp, I read through this quickly. Even though it started off a bit slow, it was great that the relationships were allowed to develop slowly and surely. I did like the world building even if it was an info dump told through story-telling around a campfire. The war between the two magical factions reminded me of Victoria Aveyard's <em>Red Queen</em> series, so if you li</span>
  <span id="freeText17550627581982098099" style="display:none">An Advance Reader Copy was provided by the publisher for review. Quotes pulled from the ARC may be incorrect and may be subject to change.<br /><br />Welp, I read through this quickly. Even though it started off a bit slow, it was great that the relationships were allowed to develop slowly and surely. I did like the world building even if it was an info dump told through story-telling around a campfire. The war between the two magical factions reminded me of Victoria Aveyard's <em>Red Queen</em> series, so if you like that world, you'd like this one. I prefer this world though. The battle in the arena reminded me so much of the movie, <em>Gladiator</em>! Except that it's a female lead. I like the main characters budding hate-to-love relationship and the gladiator style battle scenes were exciting to read.<br /><br />As for the characters, I thought Ruby was a bit slow on piecing things together. She also seems to cry a lot and thinks of herself as weak, when in reality you know she's not. She reminded me of <em>X-Men</em>'s Jean Grey and the Phoenix. I think this was done on purpose so we could see how she grows as a character. Here's hoping her character develops in the next book. The chemistry between Ruby and Arcus was super hot. I found myself swooning at times and I really liked their relationship. My fave romances are always hate-to-love and this was one of my favourites.<br /><br />A wonderful fantasy debut written by a fellow Canadian, I couldn't put it down until it was finished. Can't wait for the next book and you'll be sure I'll be requesting an ARC of the next book.<br /><br />RATING 4/5<br /><br />QUOTES<br /><br />"If you hurt me, I'll burn you do badly even your mistress will run in terror." (26)<br /><br />"I'm no danger to anyone but the people who hurt me." (44)<br /><br />"If we all had names to suit us, you'd be called Thorn in My Backside. Or Plague of the Gods.<br />And you'd be Miserable Blockhead." (85)<br /><br />"Why would anyone want to stir up hatred when there was so much already?" (177)<br /><br />"Your touch hurts me, too. But it's a pain I enjoy." (302)<br /><br />"There is always light in darkness. It may only be a pinpoint, but it is there. Follow it and you will find your way free." (309)<br /><br />"When it comes to you, I like to be burned." (371)</span>

<div id="review_1516695584" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1516695584" />
    <a title="Sophie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8563233-sophie"><img alt="Sophie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564510350p2/8563233.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1516695584?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophie" href="/user/show/8563233-sophie">Sophie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781473635173" href="/book/show/31134210-frostblood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8563233-sophie?shelf=own-read">own-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8563233-sophie?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8563233-sophie?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8563233-sophie?shelf=2017-releases">2017-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8563233-sophie?shelf=arcs-read">arcs-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1516695584" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1454060845098492185">I received an Advance Reader Copy from the publisher. This in no way impacted on my view.<br/><br/>This book was amazing! I don't know how good this review will be, because I just loved the book so much. The first in a new series, Frostblood follows our heroine, Ruby, who is a Fireblood in a world of Frostblood’s. Her country is ruled by the wicked Frost King, who has his minions seek out and destroy any Fireblood about. Hiding her powers for years, she unwittingly draws the soldiers to her village, and h</span>
  <span id="freeText1454060845098492185" style="display:none">I received an Advance Reader Copy from the publisher. This in no way impacted on my view.<br /><br />This book was amazing! I don't know how good this review will be, because I just loved the book so much. The first in a new series, Frostblood follows our heroine, Ruby, who is a Fireblood in a world of Frostblood’s. Her country is ruled by the wicked Frost King, who has his minions seek out and destroy any Fireblood about. Hiding her powers for years, she unwittingly draws the soldiers to her village, and her mother is killed. On the run, she meets a mysterious Frostblood warrior, Arcus, and seeks refuge in a local monastery. There, she begins to learn how to use her powers, and with the help of Arcus, begins to become strong enough to fight back.<br /><br />The world building in this book was fantastic. Considering it’s a debut by Blake, I was overwhelmed with the language and descriptive techniques used. Though it’s been touted as similar to Red Queen and Throne of Glass, I found it blew them both out of the water. Honestly, I was mesmerised from the first page, until the last.<br /><br />The main characters, Ruby and Arcus, were extremely fleshed out, and their characterisations seemed perfect, for their stories. Ruby is headstrong, and doesn’t take to criticism and her training well, to begin with. All she wants is revenge against the Frost King and his army, and she doesn’t really care if she dies doing it. However, she’s one of the strongest Frostblood’s that has ever been seen, and there’s more riding on her than simply revenge. Arcus was brooding, and aloof, but as the book progressed, we learned more and more about him. I had guessed who he was quite early on, but still enjoyed learning more about him. <br /><br />The romance was fairly none existent for the most part of the book, but in the best way. It was that kind of slow burning romance that makes you want to scream and swoon at the sometime. I’m hoping that in book 2, well see a lot more of the romantic side of the story.<br /><br />Thank you, Hodder and Chapter 5, for my ARC. I’m just a bit gutted that I read the book so early, because it means the wait for book 2 is that much longer.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1454060845098492185" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1747183478" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1787323032659173158">3.75/5 - This review can also be found on my blog, <a href='http://danaandthebooks.com/2017/02/10/review-frostblood-elly-blake/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dana and the Books</a><br/><br/><br/>I've mentioned it before, but my weakness is characters overthrowing the governing power. I've also been reading a ton of YA fantasy lately so naturally Frostblood has been on my radar for a while now.<br/><br/>Since moving to England I get 10x more excited whenever Canada is mentioned anywhere, and with author Elly Blake being Canadian, I got extra eager to read it.<br/><br/><a href='http://danaandthebooks.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/giphy.gif' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1486759489ra/21947922.gif' alt='' width='423' height='260' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Overall, Frostblood was an enjoyable read and a solid addition to th</span>
  <span id="freeText1787323032659173158" style="display:none">3.75/5 - This review can also be found on my blog, <a href="http://danaandthebooks.com/2017/02/10/review-frostblood-elly-blake/" rel="nofollow noopener">Dana and the Books</a><br><br><br>I've mentioned it before, but my weakness is characters overthrowing the governing power. I've also been reading a ton of YA fantasy lately so naturally Frostblood has been on my radar for a while now.<br><br>Since moving to England I get 10x more excited whenever Canada is mentioned anywhere, and with author Elly Blake being Canadian, I got extra eager to read it.<br><br><a href="http://danaandthebooks.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/giphy.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1486759489ra/21947922.gif" alt="" width="423" height="260" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Overall, Frostblood was an enjoyable read and a solid addition to the YA fantasy genre. While some parts were predictable, I spent a great couple evenings doing nothing but turning the pages, engrossed in Ruby's story. The pacing didn't slow down throughout so you can fly through it quickly - it's the perfect book for a Saturday afternoon binge read!<br><br>The first 100 pages were jam packed with information and events, but the writing was solid so following along wasn't difficult or confusing.<br><br>However, a lot of YA fantasy cliches appeared throughout:<br><br>- Guardian dies leaving main character all alone<br>- Brooding YA Hero who clashes with main character<br>- Wise man<br>- Trains to use powers<br>- Prophecy<br>- Chosen one<br>- Arena battle<br><br>I am 100% fine with cliches as long as they are done well, and I do feel in Frostblood they were good additions to the story. Apart from one: the Arcus/Ruby romance story line. I know some readers live for the ships, but I'd rather have no romance at all than a seemingly forced romance. Their romance subplot felt strained and compulsory rather than natural and genuine.  After the halfway point in the book, I would skimmed those scenes until the main plot came back.<br><br><a href="http://danaandthebooks.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/tumblr_inline_ok2tp8YqaG1tnx7ex_500.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1486759489ra/21947923.gif" alt="" width="400" height="331" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I originally received an eARC via NetGalley in exchange for a review, but I just couldn't resist picking up a copy when I went back to Canada in January. So my review is of the finished Canadian copy rather than the eARC.<br><br>It's out now! (<a href="https://www.bookdepository.com/Frostblood-Elly-Blake/9781473635173/?a_aid=DanaAndTheBooks" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Depository</a> / <a href="http://amzn.to/2kkjdft" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon US</a> / <a href="http://amzn.to/2kv3c8E" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon Canada</a> / <a href="http://amzn.to/2kWgTv6" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon UK</a>)</span>

<div id="review_1697825657" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1697825657" />
    <a title="Nastassja" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7734134-nastassja"><img alt="Nastassja" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596034018p2/7734134.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1697825657?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nastassja" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nastassja" href="/user/show/7734134-nastassja">Nastassja</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/30246667-frostblood">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Nastassja by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/50252854-dabear">DaBear</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=1st-pov">1st-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=excellent-writing">excellent-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=sugar-overdose">sugar-overdose</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=best-young-adult">best-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=dark-haired-heroine">dark-haired-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=cover-ecstasy">cover-ecstasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=intiguing-concept">intiguing-concept</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1697825657" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9881486373028532437"><p><b>Actual rating: 3.5 stars</b><br/><i><b><blockquote>But history could be twisted and warped to suit the person telling it.</blockquote></b></i><br/>From the first sight <i>Frostblood</i> might seem like nothing special; something that we all have read before: a girl with special powers that are either dangerous or forbidden and she has to hide them. A tragic story that drives a girl to fight her oppressors. A hot guy who helps her. And so one. But under all the visible cliches there's <i>a hidden gem</i>. Yes, I want to call this book a hidden gem, because I fin</p></span>
  <span id="freeText9881486373028532437" style="display:none"><p><b>Actual rating: 3.5 stars</b><br /><i><b><blockquote>But history could be twisted and warped to suit the person telling it.</blockquote></b></i><br />From the first sight <i>Frostblood</i> might seem like nothing special; something that we all have read before: a girl with special powers that are either dangerous or forbidden and she has to hide them. A tragic story that drives a girl to fight her oppressors. A hot guy who helps her. And so one. But under all the visible cliches there's <i>a hidden gem</i>. Yes, I want to call this book a hidden gem, because I find it to be <b>one of the best debut novels I've read this year</b> (I know the year is still young, but something tells me my opinion won't change in the end). <br /><br />The story is about a girl <i>Ruby</i>. She lives in a world of Frostbloods - a ruling class with the named abilities to control cold. And Ruby is a <i>Fireblood</i> - controls fire, so you can imagine that Frostbloods are not happy about her abilities, because fire and cold are opposites that can't coexist in that world. The girl hides her powers from the world, training in secret, but one day soldiers arrive at her village and kill Ruby's mother in cold blood right in front of the girl, and then take Ruby to prison. After moths locked away in cold and humiliation, two strangers arrive and propose a deal to Ruby: they will free her if she agrees to help them kill the King, the one who orchestrated the hunt after the Firebloods that lead to the extinction of almost the whole species. Ruby agrees, but, of course, there's always more to the deal, and Ruby doesn't know a first thing about the war and what she's risking agreeing to be a part of.<br /><br /><b><u>PROS:</u></b><br /></p><p><b>The world-building is amazing.</b> Granted, we don't see a lot of the world around in book 1, but we learn a lot through stories and myths. <b>The myth part is fascinating</b> from he capital A. I always had weakness when it comes to stories inside the stories. There's something enchanting in reading about the stories that live in myth and veiled with mystery, and the waiting for them to come alive and be part of the real world inside the story is overwhelming. And in the case of Frostblood these myths are coming alive, and apart from telling us the history of the world, they are telling us about the possible future. <br /><br />Right and wrong side of the story. If you have noticed I chose my head-quote for a reason. As we all are well aware <b>history is written by the victors</b>. In this book we see that people hate Firebloods, because they were taught to hate them. And Ruby hates Frostbloods, because they hunt and destroy her people. Both sides are convinced in their righteousness. <i>The truth is in the eye of the beholder.</i> But real life is more gray than black or white. And we'll learn very soon Fire and Cold can work together if only they'd let go of their mutual hatred and prejudices.<br /><br /><b>This book was brutal.</b> From the first pages when soldiers killed Ruby's mother and till the end the story was filled with blood and suffering. It was emotionally hard for me to read about what the heroine went through mentally and physically (nothing in a rape category, though). The descriptions were pretty vivid, but not gory enough to make me cringe. I had a <b>Gladiator movie vibe</b>, considering that there's <i>Gladiator fights</i> in the book and the mood was pretty suiting. So if you are looking for un-sugarcoated young-adult fantasy, than Frostblood is your thing!<br /><i><blockquote>Stillness was a kind of violence in the hands of people who played at handing out pain.</blockquote></i><br />The heroine - <b><i>Ruby</i> was easy for me to relate with.</b> I sympathize with the girl instantly. This is a first person narration and it can be tricky, because you are stuck in a character's head for a whole book, and if there's no connection than you'd either hate the person (looking at you Mare) or feel nothing, which is even worse, I think. And I believe, because of Ruby I connected with the story from the first pages, which happens rarely to me so early on in a book. The other thing that I liked about Ruby is that she goes after what she wants, but she doesn't feel like a hero of martyr. She wants revenge, but she thinks of people who could get hurt in the process. I can't not respect a person like that: <b>selfish, yes, but not egocentric.</b><br /><i><blockquote>I wasn’t being noble. There was nothing noble about a thirst for revenge. It was about getting what I wanted, a chance to kill the king. And no one else would have to suffer because of me.</blockquote></i><br />Plus the girl is a healer; she was raised to value life, to preserve it. She doesn't want to kill, but it doesn't mean she won't have to, because she does and she kills, but she values the lives she takes and always looks for a way without killing anyone. Alas to kill or not to kill often did not depend on Ruby's willingness, because <i>arena</i> is a place where you either kill or be killed. As I said, a brutal book!<br /><br />I liked the romance, the first stage of the romance, to be exact. I adored Ruby's and Arcus's bickering. <b>From enemies to lovers is one of my favorite tropes</b> and I never - never - say no to a sizzling chemistry between two characters.<br /><i><blockquote>“If we all had names to suit us, you’d be called Thorn in My Backside. Or Plague of the Gods.”<br />I prickled at his scathing tone. “And you’d be Miserable Blockhead.”<br />“Is that the best you can do?”“Give me time. I’m half frozen.” &lt;..&gt; “Perhaps your name should be Icy Tyrant. No, wait. Frigid Despot.”</blockquote><br /><blockquote>“You speak as if I’m as heavy as an ox,” I said. “Last week I was a bundle of sticks.”<br />“You’re still too thin.”<br />“Perhaps if I gain some weight, you won’t call me a stick anymore.”<br />“You may hope to one day be a branch.” <br />I glanced at him sharply, unable to repress a little flutter of delight that he was bothering to joke with me.“A log, even,” I suggested.<br />“Doubtful,” he said wryly.</blockquote></i><br />I loved the easy-going relationship they had. Ruby and Arcus spent months together, and there wasn't insta anything between them, but a gradual getting to know each other, then trust, friendship and love.<br /><br /><b>The writing keeps you glued to the pages.</b> It is definitely commendable for the author, because it is her debut novel and such level of masterly is not often met even in more experienced authors. The way <i>Elly Blake</i> tells her story, especially the myths part, is fascinating. <br /><br /><u><b>CONS:</b></u><br /></p><p><b>Second half of the book was a little bit sagging</b>. Some of the characters' actions made me doubt the logic of such decisions, but it is the first part in a trilogy (?), so I will forgive the author for some extremity, and will wait to see how the author continues her story in book 2. <br /><br /><b>The romance turned into a sugarcoated glue in the second part of the book.</b> It was my biggest disappointment after such a lovely start, and probably the main reason I couldn't give the book full 4 stars. It felt like <b>one started a race but dropped dead sheer meters form the finish line.</b> You can't give me such drive between characters and then turn it into mash. I blame the urgency with which the author jumped into romantic jungles and turned a perfect chemistry into a perfect sugar overdose. I lost all the joy from Ruby and Arcus as a couple, but I really hope the spark will return. So far I insist on my belief that the author rushed the romantic part too early; maybe she should've tortured us with angst a little bit longer? Of course, it might be just me and my tastes, and other people will find the romance suiting or might not like it from the beginning and won't feel any discomfort at all if they don't care for Ruby and Arcus as a couple.<br /><br /><b>There's cliches in this book</b>, especially the once in the romance part: he smells divinely, his eyes shine with thousand of colors and so one. Plus some move plots were pretty obvious, but that, overall, didn't spoil my general enjoyment of the book.<br /><br /><u><b>Bottom line:</b></u> Definitely recommend this book if you are looking for a light but not silly YA fantasy with interesting world and nice characters. Plus the writing is lovely. I'd say if you enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22328546.Red_Queen__Red_Queen___1_" title="Red Queen (Red Queen, #1) by Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Queen</a>, this book might be to your liking too. If you didn't like <i>Red Queen</i>, then you have even more reasons to read <i>Frostblood</i>, because, in my opinion, it is better than the aforementioned queen.</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="9881486373028532437" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1815038679" />
    <a title="Alyssa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa"><img alt="Alyssa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500935920p2/8472395.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1815038679?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyssa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyssa" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa">Alyssa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8472395-alyssa?shelf=2017-releases">2017-releases</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1815038679" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6241057088755633302">***<a href='http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2016/11/review-frostblood-by-elly-blake.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br/><br/>Frostblood by Elly Blake<br/>Book One of the Frostblood Saga series<br/>Publisher: Little, Brown Books for Young Readers<br/>Publication Date: January 10, 2017<br/>Rating: 4 stars<br/>Source: ARC sent by the publisher<br/><br/>Summary (from Goodreads):<br/><br/>Seventeen-year-old Ruby is a fireblood who must hide her powers of heat and flame from the cruel frostblood ruling class that wants to destroy all that are left of her kind. So when her mother is killed for protecting her and rebel fros</span>
  <span id="freeText6241057088755633302" style="display:none">***<a href="http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2016/11/review-frostblood-by-elly-blake.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br /><br />Frostblood by Elly Blake<br />Book One of the Frostblood Saga series<br />Publisher: Little, Brown Books for Young Readers<br />Publication Date: January 10, 2017<br />Rating: 4 stars<br />Source: ARC sent by the publisher<br /><br />Summary (from Goodreads):<br /><br />Seventeen-year-old Ruby is a fireblood who must hide her powers of heat and flame from the cruel frostblood ruling class that wants to destroy all that are left of her kind. So when her mother is killed for protecting her and rebel frostbloods demand her help to kill their rampaging king, she agrees. But Ruby's powers are unpredictable, and she's not sure she's willing to let the rebels and an infuriating (yet irresistible) young man called Arcus use her as their weapon.<br /><br />All she wants is revenge, but before they can take action, Ruby is captured and forced to take part in the king's tournaments that pit fireblood prisoners against frostblood champions. Now she has only one chance to destroy the maniacal ruler who has taken everything from her and from the icy young man she has come to love.<br /><br />Fast-paced and compelling, Frostblood is the first in a page-turning new young adult three-book series about a world where flame and ice are mortal enemies—but together create a power that could change everything. <br /><br />What I Liked:<br /><br />Here it is, folks - my first 2017 book review! After receiving a review copy, I couldn't wait to read Frostblood, so it's very fitting that this would be a review of my first 2017-published book. And even better - this book did not disappoint me!<br /><br />Ruby is a Fireblood, and possibly one of the last in existence. Firebloods have been wiped out by Frostbloods. The king is a powerful Frostblood, aided by the power of an ancient evil. Ruby is discovered by the king's soldiers, the soldiers kill her mother, and take Ruby to a prison. When two frostbloods come to the prison to break her out in exchange for her help with taking down the frostblood king, Ruby is cautious but she agrees. She has despised frostbloods since her mother's murder, but the monks who take her in are not so bad. Neither is the warrior young man who assists the monks in breaking her out of prison. As Ruby trains to become stronger to defeat the evil power that is fueling the king, she begins to realize that she has a lot more to lose than she thought. But she will fight to protect the ones she has grown to love, and destroy anyone in her path.<br /><br />This book started off shockingly (with Ruby's capture and her mother's murder), and I was hooked from that point onward. There are so many scene shifts in the book, so many settings, and so much action. You know how usually the protagonist in a fantasy novel will be in one setting for about half the book, and then after he/she "learns" everything important, he/she goes off to battle? Not quite the setup, in this book. I was on board with this! There were many changes of scenery, and the while Ruby is at the monastery for a good amount of time, she isn't there for the majority of the book.<br /><br />I was so impressed with the characterization and character development in this book. Ruby is feisty and brash, qualities you might expect to see in a fire wielder. Arcus, the frostblood who helps break out Ruby and train her at the monastery, seems cold and impervious, just like you'd expect from an ice wielder. <br /><br />I adored Ruby. She's a little impulsive and temperamental, and she has a very difficult time controlling her fire. I liked her feisty attitude, and sharpness of her retorts, and how she wouldn't take crap from anyone. Ruby is not weak, though she is vulnerable more than once in the book. She fights for herself and for others. At first she might seem selfish, but it makes sense, given how long she was in prison. And she becomes selfless and noble, as the book goes on.<br /><br />Arcus is arguably the second protagonist of the book. The book is told from Ruby's first-person POV, but I think Arcus is just as important. He isn't a monk, but he lives with them. From the start, he and Ruby clash and do not get along. They push and pull, argue and bicker, and it really seemed like they hated each other. Arcus is impatient and stern, mysterious and hardened. I liked Arcus despite how hard he was on Ruby, initially. He had good reason to be hard on her, though reading from Ruby's POV might convince you otherwise. Arcus has a difficult past that he doesn't like to talk about, which makes him all the more mysterious. But once we find out his entire story, I wanted to hug him. He has had to live with quite a bit of tragedy - no wonder he wanted to be like the ice he creates.<br /><br />How could I not mention the romance, after talking about those two? I loved the romance in this book. They are fire and ice - literally. I have always loved the idea of opposites attract, AND I love hate-to-love romance, plus all the arguing/banter... there is a lot of tension and passion between these two, and it spills over. But it's not just their natures clashing - their personalities are the exact opposite and it's so fun to watch unfold. I hope there will be more romantic clashes in future books, because this book certainly did not have enough! Also, no love triangle.<br /><br />The story was sweeping and captivating, and had me engrossed from the start. I could not put this book down! Go figure, I started reading it around midnight. And I did not stop reading it until I was finished! It was that good.<br /><br />I love fantasy, and I love how different and intriguing this fantasy was. The world-building was well-written, and I liked how much history of the kingdom that the author included. I liked that prophecies weren't too heavy in this book, though there were a few floating around. The author set up a really epic fantasy story, and I was impressed.<br /><br />I am beyond excited to get my hands on the second book! While I thought this book ended perfectly and could stop there, I'm excited to see where the author will go with the story.<br /><br />What I Did Not Like:<br /><br />More tug-of-war between Arcus and Ruby! Their interactions are part of some of my favorite scenes in this book. I hope Ruby never loses her hot temper and spunk, and I hope Arcus never loses his imperious uptight-ness! <br /><br />Would I Recommend It:<br /><br />If you enjoy YA high fantasy, then I definitely recommend this book. It's good stuff, very fresh and engrossing and entertaining. I would have loved it as a standalone, but it's cool that it's part of a series. High fantasy is my favorite genre, and so I'm usually even more critical, with high fantasy. But this book really pleased me!<br /><br />Rating:<br /><br />4.5 stars. I have no good reason for rounding down, other than I'm picky. But seriously, this book was incredible! I had a feeling that I would like it, but I really really liked it. I hope the next book does not disappoint me!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6241057088755633302" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer8270786867993931169">I reread this to remind myself of everything before I read Fireblood. I'm really scared and excited and ADFHDGNKJDNSFI!!!!!!!<3<3<3<br/><br/><b>Original Review:</b><br/><br/>Oh. My. Goodness. This book was incredible! I can't believe that I have to wait until September for the next one... <br/><br/>Elly Blake has an incredible writing style. The words flowed off the page and all the characters were so well written and developed. This is young adult fantasy at it's peak, I can't believe this book isn't more widely renowned! I was ex</span>
  <span id="freeText8270786867993931169" style="display:none">I reread this to remind myself of everything before I read Fireblood. I'm really scared and excited and ADFHDGNKJDNSFI!!!!!!!&lt;3&lt;3&lt;3<br /><br /><b>Original Review:</b><br /><br />Oh. My. Goodness. This book was incredible! I can't believe that I have to wait until September for the next one... <br /><br />Elly Blake has an incredible writing style. The words flowed off the page and all the characters were so well written and developed. This is young adult fantasy at it's peak, I can't believe this book isn't more widely renowned! I was excited about every page, and finished it in less than a day. I couldn't stop reading, and now I could talk about this book forever! The book is fast-paced and it has a great plot all the way through. It doesn't drag on or end abruptly as many books seem to do these days. In case you couldn't tell, I really loved this book. :D<br /><br />Ruby and Arcus are such great characters, and I love how Ruby is so unpredictable. She's not helpless or overly dependant on others as some female protagonists seem to be. I loved how she was able to take control of a situation, but could also be vulnerable at times. She can sometimes be temperamental and aggressive, but she learns from her mistakes quickly and is also aware of the fact that she has these problems. It was nice that she was not a natural at everything she tried, but had to put in serious effort and hard work before she could achieve her results. She was likeable and easy to root for throughout the novel.<br /><br />Arcus seems mysterious and has such great character development throughout the novel. He is extremely loyal to the monks and the people. He truly cared about the well-being of others, hence the fact that he was hesitant to trust Ruby at first. He was not impulsive, and rarely let his feelings dictate his actions. It was nice to see how this quiet, serious character developed throughout the book.<br /><br />I think it is really the characters that make the book so un-put-downable. They are unique and work well together in the given circumstances. The plot and the setting were also brilliant, but really I think the reason I liked it so much was because the characters are so well written and I really wanted to know what happened to them at every twist and turn. <br /><br />The history of the world that they were in was rich, and very well explained. You were not immediately overwhelmed by too many details being thrown at you all at once, but there was also so many cool things about the world that are beautifully explained. <br /><br />Some people have criticised this book for being predictable; but I personally did not find it so. I was enthralled by the plot, ideas and concepts throughout, despite a few clichés and familiar tropes. After spending her whole life in hiding, Ruby goes to avenge her people; right into the heart of the enemy. The constant struggle of choosing who to trust and the struggles of controlling her power guide the storyline, and the book was so thrilling. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Ruby and Arcus are so cute together at the end, I love it! Their relationship has the perfect balance between being realistic, but also really cute and swoon-worthy. Also, Arcus' big reveal in the arena was so incredible; I never saw it coming!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />To anybody who is thinking about reading this book; I highly recommend that you give it a go. ;D</span>

<div id="review_1918807936" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1918807936" />
    <a title="Caitlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57334157-caitlin"><img alt="Caitlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507948675p2/57334157.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1918807936?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caitlin" href="/user/show/57334157-caitlin">Caitlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781473635180" href="/book/show/33593802-frostblood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57334157-caitlin?shelf=2017-read">2017-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57334157-caitlin?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57334157-caitlin?shelf=anticipated-2017-release">anticipated-2017-release</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1918807936" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15363119958443169459"><b>
  <i>"There is always light in darkness. It may only be a pinpoint, but it is there. Follow it and you will find you way free."</i>
</b><br/><br/><b>Wow wow wow wow wow</b><br/><br/>4.5/5 stars <br/><br/>Wow. It's been over 12 hours since I finished this book and I'm honestly still thinking about it and trying to process this. When I first picked this book up 2 days ago, I put it on hold at chapter 7 because I was bored and it was putting me in a slump. I honestly had low hopes for this book but damn it blew my expectations out of the water </span>
  <span id="freeText15363119958443169459" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"There is always light in darkness. It may only be a pinpoint, but it is there. Follow it and you will find you way free."</i>
</b><br><br><b>Wow wow wow wow wow</b><br><br>4.5/5 stars <br><br>Wow. It's been over 12 hours since I finished this book and I'm honestly still thinking about it and trying to process this. When I first picked this book up 2 days ago, I put it on hold at chapter 7 because I was bored and it was putting me in a slump. I honestly had low hopes for this book but damn it blew my expectations out of the water when I picked it back up again yesterday. I'm so glad I gave this another shot and I'm already beginning the count down for book two (luckily it's only 7 months away). I completely understand why a lot of people didn't find this book amazing because it was a bit stereotypical YA fantasy, but it honestly didn't bother me. I really loved this and I'd definitely recommend going into this book aware of the mixed reviews, but still with an open mind.<br><br>I'm sure you can read the blurb for yourself, but basically Ruby is a fireblood which means she's in control of fire and it's basically her entire being and she's been hunted her whole life by the frostbloods who are the opposite of her because they have an old rivalry. She gets taken by the frostbloods from her village where her mother is killed and she gets thrown in a prison. She then gets brother out by 2 men: Brother Thistle and Arcus who take her back to their 'camp' basically. Here she trains to control her fire in order to eventually defeat the Frost King.<br><br>The big stand out in this book was definitely the characters. Even though I forgot <b>Ruby's</b> name a solid 10 times, I loved her character. She's definitely not what you expected and there's more to her than meets the eye. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Early on it's discussed that Ruby may be the daughter of light, however, she ends up being the daughter of darkness which is honestly so intriguing and I can't wait to see more of her development. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Look, I'm trash for a strong intimidating warrior who trains our main female character. That is the type of guys I love in books and I'm not afraid to admit it. <b>Arcus</b> was the embodiment of everything I love in a male main character. He's a guarded powerful warrior with a dark and twisted path who would die for Ruby and if that doesn't make you weak at the knees, I don't know what does. He's a precious cinnamon roll and I basically spent the entire book squealing about my love for him. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1486108854ra/21881925.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441833237ra/16157505.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It's discovered early on that Arcus has some pretty serious scars and he hides his face almost entirely by a cloak for a large portion of this book. When his face is finally 'revealed' we find out that his face is covered in burn marks. <br><br><b>
  <i>"What are you hiding?"<br>"I'm hiding nothing. I only cover what people don't wish to see."</i>
</b><br><br>I feel like Arcus' comments about his scars were so raw and real and I was honestly so broken every time he mentioned about how self conscious they made him. He's honestly such a precious baby and <b>I will protect him with my life</b>. Arcus deserves the world and I will attack those who take it away from him. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[When Ruby finds out that Arcus 'dies' my heart shattered and I was in crazy denial. Thank god that he's okay because I would've sued. HOWEVER, THEN THE BIG REVEAL HAPPENS. <b><u>ARCUS IS ARELIUS ARKANUS</u></b> WHO IS THE RIGHTFUL KING TO THE THRONE BUT HIS BROTHER TRIED TO KILL HIM AND HIS BROTHER FAILED BECAUSE HE IS HERE ALIVE AND READY TO TAKE BACK HIS THRONE AND I SPENT THE ENTIRE LAST SECTION OF THIS BOOK SCREAMING BECAUSE I DIDN'T SEE THAT COMING AT ALL. We've seen so many lost princesses but A LOST KING?! OH MY GOD  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Arcus and Ruby's relationship melts my heart and I need more. Book 2 blurb hints at a love triangle emerging and honestly <b>
  <u>if anything happens to this ship I will scream. </u>
</b><br><br><b>
  <i>"My bundle of firewood," he said softly. "It's good to have you in my arms again."</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1465852219ra/19408747.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="15363119958443169459" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1836697441" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1836697441" />
    <a title="Chelsies Reading Escape" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16445884-chelsies-reading-escape"><img alt="Chelsies Reading Escape" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569611204p2/16445884.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1836697441?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsies Reading Escape" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsies Reading Escape" href="/user/show/16445884-chelsies-reading-escape">Chelsies Reading Escape</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16445884-chelsies-reading-escape?shelf=review-books">review-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16445884-chelsies-reading-escape?shelf=canadian-authors">canadian-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16445884-chelsies-reading-escape?shelf=amazing-books">amazing-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16445884-chelsies-reading-escape?shelf=series-to-finish">series-to-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1836697441" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8108081116440784542">I flew through this book once I actually had the time to sit down and read it. I read most of it within a day. The story is about a fireblood who is being hunted by the frostblood King when shes taken in by monks who teach her to control her powers. I love elemental magic and this book did it well. The beginning starts off with a bang but the second part of the book has a lot more action. I still liked the world building and getting to know the characters in the first part.<br/><br/>I thought the characte</span>
  <span id="freeText8108081116440784542" style="display:none">I flew through this book once I actually had the time to sit down and read it. I read most of it within a day. The story is about a fireblood who is being hunted by the frostblood King when shes taken in by monks who teach her to control her powers. I love elemental magic and this book did it well. The beginning starts off with a bang but the second part of the book has a lot more action. I still liked the world building and getting to know the characters in the first part.<br /><br />I thought the characters were really captivating. I liked Ruby perspective. Her insecurities and struggles to control her powers made her more relatable. I typically prefer characters who are more confident but Ruby still had a fierce attitude that I really enjoyed. Her time in the castle was compelling. I wasnt a big fan of Arcus at first but I grew to love him once I got to know him better. I thought Brother Thistle and Gamut as well as Marella were great side characters.<br /><br />It usually rubs me the wrong way when love interests arent nice to each other but it wasnt too bad in this book. They start out hating each other but once they admit their feelings they're arent as mean to one another. I actually found myself rooting for them and I got excited when they had cute moments together. I want to see them spend more time together. I was able to predict the character twist but that didnt bother me. I was actually happy to be proven right.<br /><br />I wouldnt read the goodreads summary because its a bit spoilery and the book is a lot better if you dont have certain expectations. I thought this was a fantastic debut by a wonderdul Canadian author. I loved the concept of a world with the firebloods and frostbloods, especially how they came to be. The visions, gods and prophecies were fascinating. The ending was satisfying and Im looking forward to the sequel.<br /><br />*received in exchange for an honest review*</span>
  <a data-text-id="8108081116440784542" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('egFgOnAwLXvHGE9CLniyC0IiRV4L7t7Rh5mkFR7O0qmH6lunmaxcKs/G/nk66/DKNS7WnoFVrmyUSvx+/rHT9A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('oLyXAaOXlk2xlLIputU5EA3CyNAyF3CEyFWYpEwNHxFdV6ycSgvnHLlKAxKuRnvRes5bELisADnbhsDPrHIeTA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
